        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer450240272">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7260243428265131301">Read this five or six times, now, and hadn't realized I hadn't put it in Goodreads until now.<br /><br />It's the seventh Watch book in the Discworld; I think it probably requires a little bit of background. This is a shame, since it's a book I love enough I would like to be able to recommend that people read it with as little wait as possible.<br /><br />It's about fear, and the problems inherent in trying to manage people, and secret police, and what you are and are not willing to give up for the right thing. History</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7260243428265131301">Read this five or six times, now, and hadn't realized I hadn't put it in Goodreads until now.<br /><br />It's the seventh Watch book in the Discworld; I think it probably requires a little bit of background. This is a shame, since it's a book I love enough I would like to be able to recommend that people read it with as little wait as possible.<br /><br />It's about fear, and the problems inherent in trying to manage people, and secret police, and what you are and are not willing to give up for the right thing. History and revolutions and how many of the things you want will be there in the morning--from Truth, Justice, and Freedom, all the way down to a hard-boiled egg. All the things you didn't know soon enough, and all the things you know now that it was easier when you didn't know.<br /><br />And cigar cases, and spoons, and the sprigs of lilac on the Glorious Twenty-Fifth of May.<br /><br />It's a very sad book, and a very happy book, and I would say the protagonist is a shining example of nobility in the face of crushing odds except that I think calling Sam Vimes <em>noble</em> is the sort of thing that gets lumped in with gilt armour and a plume allowance. But he is a good man. This is too rare, and too quiet, and very fine.<br /><br />It's a lovely book. One of my favourites.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review nosyndicate" id="review_1229743207">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1229743207" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/3149418-sigrid-ellis" class="left imgcol" title="Sigrid Ellis"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1289178923p2/3149418.jpg" alt="Sigrid Ellis" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/1229743207?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Mar 17, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/3149418-sigrid-ellis" class="user" title="Sigrid Ellis">Sigrid Ellis</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/47989.Night_Watch" title="Paperback 9780552154307" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/3149418-sigrid-ellis?shelf=fiction-fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fiction-fantasy</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1229743207">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5348813875597367660">This is the first Pratchett book I have liked.<br /><br />I like it because Sam Vimes is a tired, practical adult insisting on plodding onwards towards decency.<br /><br />I'm just too old for most books about teenagers and young adults out on their first forays in the world. When I was younger I read those books voraciously. I needed those stories. I craved them. But I'm older now, different now, and I find that the stories I want have also changed.<br /><br />I like Vimes. I like him because he knows how desperately fucked-up th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5348813875597367660">This is the first Pratchett book I have liked.<br /><br />I like it because Sam Vimes is a tired, practical adult insisting on plodding onwards towards decency.<br /><br />I'm just too old for most books about teenagers and young adults out on their first forays in the world. When I was younger I read those books voraciously. I needed those stories. I craved them. But I'm older now, different now, and I find that the stories I want have also changed.<br /><br />I like Vimes. I like him because he knows how desperately fucked-up things can get and he understands that this is no kind of reason to quit trying.<br /><br />The choice is not between doing good and doing evil, it's between doing good and doing nothing.<br /></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5348813875597367660">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/2028832-kathleen?shelf=fantasy" class="actionLinkLite">fantasy</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2028832-kathleen?shelf=fiction" class="actionLinkLite">fiction</a>, 
              <a href="/review/list/2028832-kathleen?shelf=read-in-2014" class="actionLinkLite">read-in-2014</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer956744591">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12792921844524231768">This is a book about fatherhood. Yet the baby is only born at the very end. This is a book about the fact that when talking to a child, adults are often only talking to the child they once were. Yet it makes the rarely stated point that it might just be best if the adult simply didn't know the hard lesson they learned from whatever mistake the child is about to make. This is a book about revolution. Yet the change that comes is slow and insufficient.<br /><br />This is a book about responsibility. And how a</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12792921844524231768">This is a book about fatherhood. Yet the baby is only born at the very end. This is a book about the fact that when talking to a child, adults are often only talking to the child they once were. Yet it makes the rarely stated point that it might just be best if the adult simply didn't know the hard lesson they learned from whatever mistake the child is about to make. This is a book about revolution. Yet the change that comes is slow and insufficient.<br /><br />This is a book about responsibility. And how appropriate it is that we finally see Sam Vimes as a Sargent-At-Arms. <br /><br />Really, every aspect of this book is perfectly crafted, the way a book about time travel has to be. Layered, thematic, cyclical, but with plenty of jokes about seamstresses and medieval doctors. <br /><br />I highly recommend this book. You may need to read a lot of other Discworld novels for it to be meaningful and make sense, but really, this book is worth the requisite investment. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12792921844524231768">...more</a>

          </span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer144855898">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10579022900814503193">String, bitter, dark and sweet (much like %85 chocolate) this book from the city watch series is a departure from all the previous Sam Vimes books. It is hard for me to be sure, but I think it might work well as a stand alone read for people who have not followed PTerry, want to get into the discworld books but find themselves unable to bond with the earlier books.<br /><br />Sam Vimes, while pursuing a particularly nasty murderer ends up on a dome of Unseen University just as magic goes haywire, he is cata</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10579022900814503193">String, bitter, dark and sweet (much like %85 chocolate) this book from the city watch series is a departure from all the previous Sam Vimes books. It is hard for me to be sure, but I think it might work well as a stand alone read for people who have not followed PTerry, want to get into the discworld books but find themselves unable to bond with the earlier books.<br /><br />Sam Vimes, while pursuing a particularly nasty murderer ends up on a dome of Unseen University just as magic goes haywire, he is catapulted back, not only in Anke Morporks history but in his own. He ends up back at a particularly important part of his own development as a watchman, during an event that was part of sealing the future of the Watch, although in an usual way.<br /><br />As I said, a bit darker and a bit more bitter than some of the earlier works, the characters are more gritty than comical and the social commentary is becoming more obvious. I really do love the way this series became more mature as you real through them.</span>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_744698825">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/744698825" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/9273490-ashton" class="left imgcol" title="Ashton"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1341334037p2/9273490.jpg" alt="Ashton" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/744698825?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 18, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/9273490-ashton" class="user" title="Ashton">Ashton</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText"> · </span>
          <a href="/book/show/833428.Night_Watch" title="Paperback 9780552148993" class="lightGreyText">review of another edition</a>


        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer744698825">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer14538107961364698981">This was the first of Pratchett's books that I ever read and I immediately fell in love with the world that he had created and this book cemented Vimes as one of my favorite characters. Coming back to it now, years later, and I appreciate it more than I did when I first read it. While it isn't necessary to read any of the Discworld books in order, I found it much more enjoyable to come to this book after reading the other books that focused on Vimes. It deepened my appreciation for the character</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText14538107961364698981">This was the first of Pratchett's books that I ever read and I immediately fell in love with the world that he had created and this book cemented Vimes as one of my favorite characters. Coming back to it now, years later, and I appreciate it more than I did when I first read it. While it isn't necessary to read any of the Discworld books in order, I found it much more enjoyable to come to this book after reading the other books that focused on Vimes. It deepened my appreciation for the character development over time. So if you haven't read the others, I would highly suggest going back and starting with the first Vimes novel with is Guards! Guards!. That being said, on to the actual review. <br /><br />Satire is a dying art and Pratchett is one of the best writers out there that gives me hope that it will continue. He is astute and aware of the world around him and draws a lot of social commentary in each of his books but the Watch books especially. At its simplest, this is a policeman novel of good guy versus bad guy, in the wrong place at the wrong time. But because this is Pratchett, nothing is simple. The wrong place at the wrong time means actually going backward in time and ending up in your own past and having to survive as someone else. I don't want to give away the plot too much but it definitely grabs the readers attention. <br /><br />Now for some people, the story in and of itself is interesting enough but for the careful reader, you'll notice a lot of social commentary that isn't pushed down your throat. I absolutely hate an author that tries to force me toward their viewpoint with obvious allegory or constantly pushing a point through their characters. This is what Pratchett avoids masterfully and makes his opinions gems that you want to deal with rather than something you want to move past as quickly as possible. They are often as short as a few lines and if you're not tuned in, you'll miss them. For instance, what makes it okay for a policeman to use force but not a criminal or is it okay? The characters brush on issues like this throughout the book and the author allows the reader to agree or disagree with his characters opinions because they aren't forced on you. If you want to think about these issues you can, or you can simply enjoy the story for what it is. That is the beautiful thing about Discworld, there is so much beauty and truth in them but at the heart they are just amazing stories. You'll laugh and cry with the characters, you'll hope and ache with their struggles, and in the end you'll be surprised how much you cared about them and how much they can change you or your perspective if you'll let them. <br /><br />I highly recommend this books, it's one of the best out of the Discworld series. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="14538107961364698981">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

    <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett">About Terry Pratchett</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett"><img alt="1654" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1235562205p2/1654.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer903576372964717069">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText903576372964717069">Sir Terry Pratchett sold his first story when he was thirteen, which earned him enough money to buy a second-hand typewriter. His first novel, a humorous fantasy entitled <em>The Carpet People</em>, appeared in 1971 from the publisher Colin Smythe. <br /><br />Terry worked for many years as a journalist and press officer, writing in his spare time and publishing a number of novels, including his first Discworld novel, <em>The Color of Magic</em>, in 1983. In 1987, he turned to writing full time. <br /><br />There are over 40 books in the Discworld series, of which four are written for children. The first of these, <em>The Amazing Maurice and His Educated Rodents</em>, won the Carnegie Medal. <br /><br />A non-Discworld book, <em>Good Omens</em>, his 1990 collaboration with Neil Gaiman, has been a longtime bestseller and was reissued in hardcover by William Morrow in early 2006 (it is also available as a mass market paperback - Harper Torch, 2006 - and trade paperback - Harper Paperbacks, 2006). <br /><br />In 2008, Harper Children's published Terry's standalone non-Discworld YA novel, <em>Nation</em>. Terry published <em>Snuff</em> in October 2011. <br /><br />Regarded as one of the most significant contemporary English-language satirists, Pratchett has won numerous literary awards, was named an Officer of the British Empire “for services to literature” in 1998, and has received honorary doctorates from University of Warwick in 1999, the University of Portsmouth in 2001, the University of Bath in 2003, the University of Bristol in 2004, Buckinghamshire New University in 2008, the University of Dublin in 2008, Bradford University in 2009, University of Winchester in 2009, and The Open University in 2013 for his contribution to Public Service.<br /><br />In Dec. of 2007, Pratchett disclosed that he had been diagnosed with Alzheimer's disease. On 18 Feb, 2009, he was knighted by Queen Elizabeth II.<br /><br />He was awarded the World Fantasy Life Achievement Award in 2010.<br /><br />Sir Terry Pratchett passed away on 12th March 2015.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="903576372964717069">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/1654.Terry_Pratchett" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Terry Pratchett...</a>
